Hello everyone.

I have been meaning to open up a new thread for a while.Although Its not the best time for me as I’m still busy with my day job, forex and helping my wife with her newly established company, I’ve decided to at least lauch this thread  as a respond to the p.m’s I’ve been getting lately from some members of forexfactory and improve it slowly by the time.

-------------------------------------------------------------

As some of you already know I was posting in Graeme’s great thread called “building euqity millipede” and I humbly but strongly advice traders to check out his thread as well as silent service method and james16 since i found them  very helpful and informative ones.

-------------------------------------------------------------

I will try to keep things very simple.Actually if they are not simple then its not tradeable.period.

K.I.S.S is probably one thing  you’ve heard most in Forex but I don’t think you heard a lot about  “how to K.I.S.S”

-------------------------------------------------------------
Some things you won’t see on my charts are:

indicators,moving averages,channels,unclear  s/r levels,repainting,illusion,delusion,teaching a life lesson through charts
what you will see are:

1.major lines along with their median lines

2.Fibonacci

3.Price action interpretation.

There is a lot of theory behind what i choose to use and what i not to choose..But I won’t go into details of this since I expect that to be revealed later on by the nature of my charts..

And one last thing before we move on is that I don’t trade for money but to be in that %5 of the traders that considered to be “succesful”.So everything I share here is free and will stay free.

But only thing I expect in return is respect to what I'm trying to do here.

So If you didn't like what you'd seen here then please find somewhere else that suits you more.

I'm just doing it for sharing.

Thank you all..

---------------------------------------------

I'll go straight to the charts but It will take me some time to figure out to put them all together..

I'll be posting one by one as I complete...

I'll be back with the charts.

p.slease be aware that any questions you are thinking to ask such as "how long you been trading this,whats your r/r is,whats the gain.....etc" won't help you to implement this approach into your trading style..

This has to be your own job to collect your own data..

My data or past performance has got nothing to do with yours in the future.

4hr is secondary price action

5min is entry

--- 帖子 #6 ---
So what we did in the first example is

We waited price to convince us about its direction on the major line..

Once we're biased that its heading down because of the shape and break of the weekly on 1.4000 level
Now we want to short on the retracement of our signal candle

We applied Fibonacci on the setup candle (weekly)

We dropped down to 4hr to observe a pullback and it happened and gave us a price action on 4hr chart.

Now we want to do the same thing on 4hr..

Again we applied our fib to catch a pullback to enter on 5min.

Here is the entry..

--- 帖子 #22 ---
Thank you all..

Today (after finishing my other works) I'll try to go into little details that shaped my trading style through my experiments.

I also want to put my trading preparation in an order to make things easier follow but for a short definition I can say that I'm trying to trade "big guys'" levels ultimately with my 5 min chart..

when price on a big number only thing I know for sure is its going to be heading to next big number no matter which direction.

This simple information means at least 1.000 pips just staying in front of you.

Another thing is once you enter as per any entry system you use you must've entered because you thought it should be heading the direction you thought..

a.If price does what you expect but only when you use large stop such as placing your stop behind the s/r levels that cost you around 100 pips..

Then your timing is not good..

b.Price don't go the direction you expect and hit your large stop in shot time.

You had wrong interpretation of the market.

c.you entered and price just started moving in your direction without looking back or with tiny pullbacks.

c is our goal..It needs good interpretation and good timing..Thats all.

and I know everybody cool with weekly and 4hr charts but not 5min..Its not my favorite but Its impossible to make entries with tight stop without small timeframes.

and 5 min's another job is to keep us away from fake price actions which is very important.It even sometimes prevents us ranging market..

We'll talk more about them through charts..

I'll try to keep this thread visual as much as I can because I believe it worths thousand words..

See you then.

--- 帖子 #23 ---
Preparation/Analysis of a trade

1.Start with weekly and try to understand its story..

Here is a story of over a year period.(Past moves covered for clarity)
Move#1

It was a massive 3000 pip move and break through all the round number in the first attempt even when it exhausted at 1.2000 level
Move#2

It started with 3 bars pattern (very typical even the gap was there) at 1.2000 level which is a reversal sign and made another price action with pin-looking bar(but also an engulfing bar at the same time) on the median line of 1.2500 level..Median lines are important for some reasons..One of them is price usually shows intention where its heading further..In this case that made a convincing bar about its intention.

If you noticed I'm not talking about trend but the action.Yes It made a 3000 pip before but the fact is you will never know which move is a main move or a pullback until it ends.

There was no guarantee at the time that price would not come back to 1.2000 level when it first started raising up to the 1.2500 level..

Indeed never came back to the level of 1.2000.
Move#3

When move#2 ended by a bullish engulfing bar I thought that was a continuation of the down move but this time price was just testing %50 level of the move#3 with a pinbar.

Major lines and fib levels (38.2,50,61,8) used to define hindsight.

this time price obeyed the fib levels and continued to move up and made a second close above 1.3000 level winning the second fight.
Move#4

this move was  a typical hit one big number+pullback+hit the next big number move...
Move#5

This all started with a very nice looking pinbar at 1.4000 level and went down to the next big number.Notice the pinbar touched the 1.3000 level and came back resulting a bullish pinbar
Move#6

We were expecting another move up but price failed to breach the median line (remember they're key levels to grasp the intended direction thus making another pinbar but opposite this time signaling moving further down
Move#7

this move taught me the same fact again that you can never bu sure about the direction.When it made the close below 1.3000 level I was too sure about the down direction.But by the very first candle which was an engulfing candle It said for the second time"no I reject going lower than this level"..I'll name this candle for "rejection candle" and take this as a setup signal to analyse further
Move#8

This move made a close above the median line which is cool for longs but also a bearish pinbar at the 61.8% of the move#

Here is the real deal...

at this point you can hold your buy from the move#8 but also playing that candle for shorts just to be prepared for both side

Move#9

You might've had opposite directions alive until this candle but now This candle telling us "okay I found my support at 1.3500 level thats why I made a engulfing candle..I didnt engulf only one bearish but 3 of them at the same time..

So this is why I'm biased long for the next week...

You need reasons to enter a trade

1.a story that makes sense

2.a good setup on the weekly

3.good setup on 4hr

4.good entry on 5 min..

--- 帖子 #28 ---
We enter our trades on 5min time-frame..

Although there is no fixed stop I use,usually its around 10 pips or less depending on my entry candle and setup.

If it stops moving after my entry I usually close it with small loss and wait until I believe it starts to move.
But all entries made at the close of the candle

Remember that you entering on 5 min but targeting >1000 pips

It may sound nonsense but I know its possible through myself.

No need to trail stops.Its a hit the big number or die at the break even issue..Sometimes this approach will save you from fake price actions as well as causing some frustrations reversing after couple hundred pips.

I'll show you my losing attempts upon new trades because of they are part of the process.

--- 帖子 #47 ---
Thank you all for your nice words...

answering the question:

Yes I put the fib on the candle you mentioned but also to the very next candle in order to cover different timezones in terms of candle setup..

The reason for this is to show you that sometimes price will make its action while you're asleep but then it makes another price action in the same direction (next bar was a bullish engulfing bar that engulfed the pinbar) you can still get in the trade because of the new setup that happened in your trading time.

--- 帖子 #56 ---
apply the fib on the setup candles only..

if you got the price action on weekly and you want to go in 4hr then put the fib on weekly setup candle then drop down to 4hr..when you get your signal on 4hr do the same but this time put it on 4hr candle and then drop down to 5 min..and enter on 5min upon a price action..

you just keep narrowing the timeframes by dropping down...

--- 帖子 #58 ---
hi ghost..thank you for your input..

First of all I make hindsight only to be able to make some low risk entries..

I am not worried whether I'm right or wrong with my hindsight..

like now I have a long position on eurusd that I took last week (its up to over 100 pips  and its at b.e now.So I have two possible scenario.

1. it dies at breakeven

2.it goes to 1.4000 or even 1.5000 level making me couple thousand pips

---------

I enter my position at my best and move it to break even after moving in  my favor (preferably >30 pips).

This is all I'm trying to achieve and rest is just a tool to achieve this goal.

One can use trend lines while others use fibs or round numbers.

I try to use less relative tools such as round numbers,single candle actions,even fib levels are relative but only reason I use them is they are  very popular and used by so many traders around the world..

But I still keep it as simple as it is by putting it on the latest swing keeping limited with only 38.2,50 and 61.8 fibs being most popular fib numbers..

--- 帖子 #88 ---
Hi Sam..

your entry gives me an opportunity to explain a very important thing which is timing vs. location...

I'm glad that your entry turned out well.But I'd like to explain what you missed in your entry.

a.4hr confirmation

b.Timing

a.4 hr confirmation is something you should've waited..Because its not efficient to trade between weekly and 5min timeframes without a transition timeframe which is being 4hr in this method..

Because of the big time gap between weekly and 5 min you are easily exposed to any sudden retracement or retests..

I used to trade  Monthly and 5min timeframe too but since the gap was huge I often found that myself trying to travel between continents with no stop over..Finally I came to a conclusion that I needed one more timeframe to make this travel easier and more smooth..

b.Timing is not of course in your hands but when your timing and direction are both right ,price doesn't look back like it did not in my entry..

But in your entry it made ups and downs for a while..
Best entry is the entry that runs away from your stop loss right after you entered..

I use tight stop because I expect my entry to be a perfect or at least good entry..If its not moving in my direction that means my direction or my timing is wrong or sometimes both are wrong..

Hope this explanation helps you why I waited to get a complete 4hr candle instead of rushing on 5min without a confirmation...
Learning a lesson from a losing trade something easy but learning a lesson when you're winning is the key.

--- 帖子 #89 ---

--- 帖子 #101 ---
second position should be moved to b.e after moving around 20-25 pips in the direction..

so you now might have two positions both locked at break even..

Another thing about the method is I try to slow down to open a new position or in this case to add more position when 4 hr candle is ending soon..

The reason for that is that there is usually a pullback at the beginning of a new 4hr candle.

We don't want to deal with pullbacks when we open/add a trade..

Pullbacks should be already passed by the time we make our entry

--- 帖子 #145 ---
If you remember my early charts I mentioned about some zones (If you don't they are still there you can check them )

opening a new position zone

adding zone

watching zone

-----------------

Now we are in a watching zone as I believe (scientifically a fact) any position we open now has a lower chance to reach to the next major line up than a position supposignly opened in a "opening a new position zone"...

and also it has lower "possible" risk/reward ratio..

So what does this mean..

That means being not eager to open another position unless there is a really good opportunity

So in this zone everything should be very convincing..

Price action,movement,timing they all have to convince me to risk my money in watching zone..

and this is of course relevant but I like to treat the market sometimes conservative and sometimes aggressive upon change of risk,possibility to reach target,location,time,price action...

We are IMHO in my watching=conservative zone...

If a setup occurs here and I miss it by being extra cautious, Its totally fine. I need to manage,categorize my risks and I know I can't catch the every single setup.

This zone part of the method is more about personnel taste..

You don't even have to go in such details.

Instead of listing all the rules and entry exit ideas I believe that learning/studying through charts always better.

It does not matter whether you are correct with your interpretation (reading story) every time or not..

my only long position has 50% chance of either dying at break even or making me couple thousand pips..

simple but powerful

--- 帖子 #186 ---
about 1 hr charts...

Sure every time frame has importance but the main goal or rule is keeping things simple..

I used to use 1 hr as well but then I realized that I don't need them as I have enough timeframes already on (weekly,4hr,5min)

but one can use monthly,daily,1hr instead of my set of timeframe..

Its all up to you..

As you already know there is a difference between method and system...

Method is what I'm trying to offer here and system is what you implement from this method and other methods into your trading style and then making your own entry,exit,stop management rules depending on your characteristics,capital size, psychology,personal taste..etc

But the best way to find out what price actions rule market is analyzing the moves around those major lines and trying to see which price actions happened just before price started moving.

same logic should be applied to the all timeframes..

--- 帖子 #231 ---
Hellow wang..

excellent summary of what I meant to say about timing and location idea in one sentence..

I had hard laugh at that video too...

Location is something  we already decided (major round numbers 1.0000 1.1000 and half round numbers like 1.1500,1.2500) because of the past price actions around those levels and not because me or any retail trader makes these level important but banks,financial companies,big investors,etc.. do.

major numbers are for setting up ultimate targets and half round numbers for adding positions and some counter trade opportunities if price signals opposite direction...

about eu target of 1.45 level I believe that area worth to watch too but my reason was not the fib of mega move down as you can see on my chart but after you said that it even makes that level even stronger in this case of course only if price is still heading up..

--- 帖子 #233 ---
Hello Red

I don't calculate zones like you mentioned since I don't use any but I prefer adding between 1.4000-1.4500 as they have higher chance of survival and better r/r than any position opened in between 1.4500-1.5000.

But as you can see my last position on eu it is at 1.36 level which is above the zone that I prefer adding but the reason is it was very convincing price action around the level of 1.3500 and gave me a good entry opportunity.

So this classification of levels is not essential part of the method maybe more about detailing personal trading style.

I can trade both aggressive and conservative ways.So those opening,adding and watching zones define my trading style..I trade most aggressive on adding zone and less aggresive on opening zone and conservative on watching/probing zone.

But this is all very personal way of trading and with any method you'll be making these type of classes based on your trading skills.

--- 帖子 #258 ---
As far as I understand the method, weekly gives us the overall picture and major levels of big round numbers/support & resistance.

We then take the 4h candle as signal candle and view this candle on a 5min chart - where we can see if a trend confirmation/rejection/retrace etc. happens.

The main reason why we drop down to a lower timeframe is the fact that we can place our stops closer to price.

Look at your chart : placing stops on that 4h chart would be very far away and require more risk capital....

===============

In the case of GBPUSD we had strong up moves and I would probably wait a bit for a retrace in case you intend to go long.

But nomask will tell you if my interpretation is correct or not.

Hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #261 ---
No problem, the thread is just starting and we will ( hopefully ) go through many examples. This will make it clearer.

Maybe if you go through Nomask´s charts and download his template.

Fact is : higher timeframe charts such as weekly, daily and 4h are much more reliable. We then  use the information from those charts to find better entries with lower risk.

However, the goal is ( as I understand it ) ultimately not to catch some 5 or 15 pips here and there ( as typical scalpers would do, with high stress ), but to get in a trend gaining much more. Nomask already gave an example for this by entering very early on 1.3567 something - see where we are today.

--- 帖子 #263 ---
Hello noer..I don't have that pair on my mt4 but seems like you had nice shorts on it.

the weekly bar that made a close below the major level is your weekly setup/hindsight bar.

we're focusing on any convincing price actions.but preferably more reliable ones..engulfing/outside bars,pinbars my favorite due to their reliability.

there is no classification between timeframes and price actions..your hindsight,price action interpretation work should be working on any timeframe..

we just expect/anticipate the same direction on three different timeframes..

nice break of a major line is a signal.If its happened by a price action at the same time then its even better...

then you put your fib on the weekly and you get a nice and smooth pullback on weekly giving you another setup on 4hr..you drop to 5 min. another nice smooth pullback on 4hr there you enter your trade..

But sometimes when move is stronger you don't get a pullback but you get a price action..don't forget that no price action no move...believe me every real move needs a real price action to get attention,to get enough move and power behind it..

Here is something I missed today because of my meetings that just ended (hopefully)..

p.s:with this method you'll be missing so many good opportunities due to 5min timeframe entries but don't let them bother you or make you just jump in wherever price is.

take them as a approval of your thinking/mindset/method working.

You don't have to make money every time that your method works.

Sometimes you'll get nasty spikes that might cost you maybe a possible thousand pips.(happened to me once)

Its all part of the game.

This is when you get frustrated by the market..

But sometimes market gets frustrated by you too.

Especially when you catch a +1000 pips with an entry that had a 5-10 pips stop loss..

--- 帖子 #276 ---
Thanks survivor..welcome to thread..

When I first started this thread I was lucky that I caught a good setup (you can find it in earlier pages of the thread) that allowed me to summarize my whole method in one live example.

This first position still alive and around 400  pips up now.But the key is I did not spend hundreds pips to establish this position  I only spent maybe 10-15 pips for couple attempts at some important levels upon good price actions on higher t.f...

if I close it now probably I get a reward 26 times bigger than my initial risk.

I find unrealistic or at least unnecessary to set up some sort of fixed risk/reward ratio..You can never know when and how much market is willing to pay you.

The concept is to open trades with small attempts around a major number and target next major number/numbers...

If eurusd makes a strong close above 1.4000 level I'll keep my current long and also I'll be trying to open new positions targeting  the next major number (1.5000)...

If I get an opposite signal at 1.4000 level I'll enter opposite position to my current position to catch next major numbers down this time..

But I'll keep both open to trap the market so it can work out in the favor of one of my positions targeting over 1000 pips..

This method requires extra discipline,patience,consistency and good entry skills on 5min timeframe..

p.s:honestly I should've had more long positions after my first entry by now but I was not able to spend enough time and add more because I was busy with my other works last couple days..

But when I'm done with this trade I'll try to recover what I did right and wrong to clarify the method better

--- 帖子 #284 ---
thanks joey.You are right about trading with such method is less stressful and sometimes its even boring  which is a good sign for a trading method.

Because boredom caused by consistency in repeated actions.This is important to trade any method successfully.

hello kdx..Any questions are welcome.

about your comment,I love trading pinbars and they're my favorite but I never rely on a pinbar by itself.

after a pinbar formed,I need to see some volume in the pinbars direction to take an action.

Because a pinbar only means indecision of market (sellers and buyers fought and they got tired but no side winner yet) which is a good sign that pullback might be ended but still we need a candle that shows us who the winner is..

In the example you asked second pinbar only makes the meaning of indecision stronger but still no obvious sign about who the winner is.

I'll post a good example of pinbar setup as I find it...

--- 帖子 #309 ---
Continuing of the money management issue..

riks/reward ratio

I don't think there is any question about risk/reward ratio since the method is about getting in trades with 5-15 pips stop (depending on the entry setup) and chasing around thousand pips (depending on your entry and where the next major number is) giving us a wide range of 20x to 300x times bigger reward eventually..

I did catch over thousand pips profit trades couple times with less than 10 pip-risked positions.most recent one was the move from 1.4 level to 1.3 on eurusd.It took me 5 weeks to reach my target.

lot size

But during your attempts to get in a move you'll have some losing attempts that will give you a clue about the lot size you should be using..

after paper trading maybe 100 trades then you can have a nice data of your maximum drawdown and average stop loss that you need to define your lot size.

my average loss is about 7 pips and the lot size that I most feel comfortable is 0.1 lot for a 5000 usd account or 1 lot for a 50k account..

some may think its too conservative but again its all up to your personality and trading skills however for a 50k account when you make your first thousand pips with a single position that's equal to 10k.

the bonus of this method is added positions after your first entry..

Graeme, the owner of the thread called "building millipede equity" has a very aggresive way of stacking which I'm impressed but don't think it fits to my trading style.when I feel comfortable with stacking aggresively maybe I can try as well but nothing soon yet.

winning rate

for sure you'll have very low winning rate while you still add some nice profits on top of your capital with that huge reward/risk ratio...

so you need to paper trade (for any method out there) the method to gather your own trading data to build up your money management.

--- 帖子 #318 ---
this method needs a weekly setup candle for our hindsight.

once we're biased in one direction then we look for a 4h price action and 5min entry off the 4hr candle.

But currently we do not have such weekly candle signaling that price moving from 1.4000 level to 1.5000 yet..

maybe just a good looking 4hr candle.

my latest weekly setup candle is the one (2011.02.13) sitting on 1.3500 level engulfing last 3 bearish candles..

However since we're dealing with very small stop loss I sometimes try testing the water with little attempts based on 4hr..

But this is not an essential part of the method and it requires extra discipline not to over trade..

It is best to wait to get a weekly confirmation first..and this is how I mainly trade.

--- 帖子 #337 ---
Hi cwl0375,

for 5min entries you could read threads that focus on entry techniques, such as " Flag-Trading with trend " or Niceguy`s " Ridiculous 7 pips system ", or " How to trade 1-2-3 effectively " ( Paulus ).

However, you will notice a big difference to Nomask, as they focus on making gains only for a few pips on the 5min, hopefully catching the right trend direction. This can be fast moving, high-stress and quite difficult when practised on its own !

So, the whole intention behind Nomask`s 5min entries ( correct me if I am wrong ) is to have a confluence of the weekly, 4h as " strength " behind our 5min entries. Big difference !

But if it is only about the technicalities of entries and hiding your stops etc. these threads might give you some help.

Don`forget to come back to us !

_________

michael

--- 帖子 #351 ---
Good morning everyone.

Yesterday I tested this pinbar with a small entry cost me -8 pips and it failed to move up during the slow market hours.

These entries are necessary to catch real and quick moves that happen not often but when it does it just shoots up with no pullback covering all small attempts and making nice profit on top.

Its preferable to have the real move upon the first price action which did not happen in eurusd last night but since the price still playing around %50 of the last week's candle, its worth to keep an eye on it.

By the way no need to be glued to the screen all day long..

just checking to see if there is any price action as every 4hr candle completed is fine.

More than this can make you over trading.

--- 帖子 #352 ---
You can use different set of timeframes like monthly,daily and 1 hr if you want..

but the reason why I only limit it to three time frames is that adding more timeframes will make you confused rather than making better entries.

and I don't use monthly candle because that means when there is a p.a I'm one month behind the move that started.I don't want to be that late.

Besides,if you get a good price action on 1hr that means you'll have a good p.a on 4hr as well maybe just 20-30 pips later but since we're usually entering on the pullbacks of 4hr candles you actually do not need to mess with 1hr timeframe.

I hardly ever use 15 mins but only when I believe there is a good chance on higher timeframes and 5 min t.f is too messy to make a good entry.

But this case does not happen more than once in couple months..

--- 帖子 #358 ---
I was doing backtesting for practice.  I notice sometimes when you put a fib on 4 hour candle then drill down to 5 minute chart that price action will move beyond the fib causing one to enter only to have it retrace and stop you out.  It seems better to almost always wait for the retrace even when price seems like it's going to keep moving before a retrace.  As you stated in previous post nomask there is almost always an overlap on the next 4 hour candle.

Also I noticed on the 4 hour chart that if you keep a fib from the last swing low (bull market) and keep correcting it as price moves up you will always be ready for the next retrace.  Right now price action is around the 61.8% fib from the last swing low on the 4 hour chart on the euro.  Since I believe we are still biased long then it seems we are in an excellent area for another entry if price action cooperates.

--- 帖子 #359 ---
Good morning everyone.

There is a possible fakeout on the weekly if this weeks candle closes below the purple level.Maybe bringing us a bearish engulfing candle which might be taken as a short setup candle

So if thats the case by the end of the week ,we can either bank the profit of long position or open a new shorts due to new setup without closing the long position.

by choosing the first way,you'll have to wait for a new long setup on the weekly to enter long.

second way is psychologically harder than the first one but possibly targets for greater reward.

you don't have to think too much about which way to go..

best way is the one you feel most comfortable.

but keep in mind that the week is not over yet.

--- 帖子 #378 ---
1 standard lot for each 50k and every other position opened only after previous position/s moved to b.e...

I don't even know what leverage my broker offers because I don't need it.

However every trader has a different way of trading.Some use tight stop  while others use large stop that determines the lot size along with your maximum drawdown.

for any method out there you get to hear "demo trade it first".

Its true but you ever thouht about why?

Its not only because you need to see whether you can trade the method or not.

More important,you need to see what's your average loss,your maximum drawndown,consecutive loss,etc..

You need your trading data to set your money management before starting to trade it live.

I don't believe %2-%3 maximum risk kind of m.m rules..To me its just too much risking for a single trade.

Honestly I don't think %5 of the traders (called succesful ones) risk that much.

my average risk is around %0.2 per trade.

So Its 10 times smaller than what I usually hear.

Hope this helps

Thank you Nomask.

Rather than extending this with different mathematical money management calculations I can say from experience :

a) I tried ultra-shortterm trading with high leverage. My thought : if I make 20 pips ( 1Pip worth 20 USD = 2 lots ) daily, that would be 400 USD. Not bad. Result : huge stress.

b) then the idea : increase my risk to reward ratio and reduce leverage. I can then trade with less lots, but the pips gained are more than 20 pips per trade. I can place larger stops if I want to, or don`t experience so much stress even if I get stopped out multiple times. This works !

Hope anyone can make sense out of that....

_____________

michael

--- 帖子 #382 ---
Good morning everyone..

Here is something little bit off the method just to point out that anything/any price action on higher timeframes can be traded in lower timeframes with low risk entries.

Although I'm biased long on eu I just took a countertrade against my hindsight.

Be aware that countertrades not necessary for any system and they need a lot of exercise before actually trading them otherwise they can take all your profits especially when you over countertrade.

I always say that first you need to master on regular rules then exceptions..

As everybody knows that when there is price gap market tends to fill that gap first before heading to its main direction.

eu started with a big gap this week (I'm not a gap trader but price action) followed by a bearish candle on the weekly trend line.and then I had this 4hr inside bar signaling possible down move.

Best place to get in a trade of an inside bar is at its top (if you entering long its at its low)

So I dropped down to 5 min and observed the high of the inside bar and entered as I got a three bar reversal there..

I moved it to b.e and this is all I expected from it.

this is my favorite when I have positions at b.e in both directions as I have a higher chance of hitting bigger target.

--- 帖子 #383 ---
what I did with the latest countertrade example was that I pretend as a day trader or a gap trader during the journey, taking advantage of their first push down but not targeting their take profit level but something possibly a lot bigger.

But the gap traders took their profits and left the market to buyers.

Thats why my only sell position died at b.e.

When it made a close back above the lower line I was expecting my position stopped out at b.e.And thats what happened.

All I need in order to make my hindsight is one weekly candle at a major level.nothing extra needed.

Its just a direction I need to choose and I don't try to interpret market via fundamentals as I  simply trade the odds with low risk entries.

--- 帖子 #391 ---
Thanks a lot...We all learning from each other..

First of,I ignore the timeframes out of my favorite three (wk,4hr,5min)

Its more important to keep things simple and clear rather  than trying to combine or consider all timeframes when trading.

I think I left this subject little bit unclear when I said I'm biased long for eu.

In fact I'm biased long for my existent position from 1.35xx and I'm not biased long for the move from the 1.4 to 1.5 yet.

Why?

Because I don't have a price action at 1.4 signaling long yet.

So if you not holding a long position currently then you better wait to get a clear signal on 1.4 to be biased long.

that means I'd be looking for a new setup for a first entry in any direction if I didn't have my long position.

any long position you enter now would be dealing with the 1.4 of major line which is bad in terms of reward/risk ratio.We don't want that.

1.attempting period

2.adding or growing profit period

3.waiting period

Hi,

I think this indicator is ideal for this model of trade. Draw horizontal levels at round numbers 1.40 1.50 and divide in half the amount of pips - 1000 500 250 125 62 and 31. You can chose how many splits you want, from 1 splits till 6.

You can also divide the chart starting from the same round numbers,  from 10 to 10 pips for other types of trade. Can add many more things I thought when I read this thread.

I like this system cos is simpler. What is difficult is to respect the rules.

--- 帖子 #412 ---
you're welcome.I'm glad to hear you enjoying the thread

What I tried to explain in my previous posts is that there is a little difference between managing an existing position from 1.35 level and opening a new position around 1.4 level to target 1.5 level.

for example when I first entered at 1.3569 my first target was 1.4 level.

But "first target" does not necessarily mean you have to close out your position(s) once its hit.

You still need to analyse the market for its direction whether to exit or stay in.

If I had no position by the last week I would have waited for week to end before making my hindsight which is the first stage of entering a trade of the method..But for managing an existing long position you can always add more as long as there is a "good setup"

After hitting the 1.4 level I did not close my long because I had no weekly candle signaling possible move down.

But If I had more than one position I may have closed some of them at that level to let my capital grow.

Hey there Nomask.  This definitly isn't my trading style of choice personally but I wanted to post in your thread to let any others reading know that this is a very top notch method of trading.  It may not be fore me because of my own personal preference but for anyone else, if you can understand it (you should be able to, it's a pretty darned simple concept) and it appeals to you, you should jump on this type of trading.

As an added bit of credibility, in my skimming of the thread I didn't see anyone refer to this term but "constant lines" have been around almost as long as charts have been.  Before all of the fancy indicators that came along like MACD, EMAs, Parabolic SARs and so on, traders used trend lines and constant lines almost exclusively.  If you're looking for a time tested method, I don't think they get any older and more reliable than this.

that weekly candle represents the direction of the sharks where they're heading (most likely).

we are being smaller fish with smaller mouths (lot size) compared to sharks (banks,fund managers,big-fat guys)

--- 帖子 #438 ---
If you remember earlier in the thread I took a 4hr candle as a setup candle wich made just a close (not a pure price action) above the previous weeks high..

Thats the reason to catch in case its a straight bold up weekly candle.

Once you biased long on the weekly

you place your fib on it but if you get an instant close above the high of the setup week then you place your fib on the 4hr and watch it in 5 min.

Because sometimes you'll get weekly candles that don't retrace but keep moving forward.

This is the way of catching them.

few posts ago I mentioned about the possibility of this week being a straight bold up candle due to the last week's shape and strong close above 1.4 level..

Sometimes we get strong weekly candles with momentum behind it.

For this type of weeks, first one or two days of the week are the only times we can enter at a nice location.

I just tried to play very simple breakout candles at minor s/r levels.

another thing for the lower line is that although I defined it as a minor s/r level Its also opening level of the weekly candle which price respects that so many times.

--- 帖子 #457 ---
correct.

1.& 2. it is just something you can't ignore if market is moving and making new highs/lows out of your weekly candle that you placed your fibs and started watching on 4hr t.f.

people love to cover most recent highs/lows thats pretty much of why I move fib to the new hi/lo points.

3.Yes we do need to  move it to the new highs and mark the previous minor s/r levels in case there is p.a or reentry opportunities

--- 帖子 #534 ---
So keep that in mind.

If the price not moving to your direction, jus leave it until it starts following your direction.

lets say You set a stop at 100 pips away for regular long term trading methods but If price not moving for you now how can you be so sure that it would start doing it in the next 5,10,50 mins or whatever it is.

When it moves in our favor we hurry to move it to b.e..

Why is that?

very same reason,there is no guarantee that it would not start moving against us in the nex couple seconds.

this is called "cut your losses short"which everybody speaks of but not everybody knows how to do it.

--- 帖子 #539 ---
one more important thing.

If you familiar with Graeme's method "building millipede" he was more aggresive than me in terms of entries.

He doesn't look for price actions and confirmations on 5min as much as I do.

I do respect his way and really impressed with his results.

But I would not apply this approach to my trading style since I feel like I am wasting too many of my bullets and having no bullet when there is a prey easy to hunt with only one bullet.

Being picky with entries not only give you low risk trades but also keeping your gun loaded all the time.

It'll cost you missing some big preys from time to time but its better than being desperate all the time.

--- 帖子 #588 ---
We need three key ingredients in order to execute an entry.

1.location

2.candle shape/price action

3.timing

location is as one of the major lines,median lines(mostly when adding),s/r levels and fib levels.

price action is

pinbars or engulfing candles which are my favorites

and rarely 3 bar reversal or an inside bar.But first two of them most reliable ones.

timing is something we do not have a control over.We just get to know after we excute the trade.when I say timing I dont' mean the market hours but when the price starts making its big bold candles.

when we get first two aligned we enter and if we get the 3rd one aligned with our entry then we get our position survived.

..

I checked the chart you posted but not all of them were descent pinbars some were "almost pinbar"..I trade almost pinbars as well but only if they respect one of the locations mentioned above.

when you trade a pinbar on higher timeframes you don't wait for confirmation as our target is risking low pips for "possibly something big" so that possible big thing we expect is suppose to start within the very next candle after the pinbar.If we can enter in the next candle and price starts moving in our favor then we get the position moved to b.e which is our first target.

BUt when you make your entry on 5min chart you can't rely on a pinbar itself since it gives you the clue that opposites losing power but no winner yet.If we get a nice confirmation candle right after the pinbar , %90 of the time its the start of a move which at least let you move your position to b.e.

you can also study more on price actions and candlestick patterns in the forum.

but use only reliable ones by checking them on your chart to see if price really followed them.

you can also classify them similar to the attached chart.

p.s:better the shape candle has more the attention it gets.

And more attention brings more momentum which determines "timing" of the method.

--- 帖子 #617 ---
Nomask --

Here's a thought, please comment and correct me if I'm wrong...

I was staring at the H4 chart and reviewing this week's move. As it's turning out, this is a bullish week and trading with the LONG bias would certainly have established our positions providing we entered those positions at the right LOCATION (1. Location, 2. candle shape/price action, 3. Timing, see http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=589).

So the question becomes, where could I have entered and my positions still survive?

First, if I stood back and stepped outside the forest, looking at the H4 candles from afar...

For a couple weeks, price was bouncing it's head on the 1.40 level, then when it finally broke, price came back down during this week to that level and retested it. If I drew a H4 S/R line off of most recent old tops (where price was meeting resistance, red line), this week's early pinbars bounced right off the Old Resistance line (old resistance becomes new support). If I could have identified that sooner, I may have paid more attention to those early in the week H4 pinbars.

Second, entries...

So where could I have entered and my positions still survive? It appears that I should be paying more attention to WICKS of DOUBLE BOTTOMS (and tops if reversed), as deepblue44 pointed out in one of his posts http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=502. Having a position on the wicks of H4 candles has a higher probability for survival with the smallest risk, thus giving us the 'trading edge' because the likelihood of price revisiting the wicks are lower than revisiting the bodies. Or another way of saying it is that we are entering long positions at 'Demand' levels, pivot points (short positions at 'Supply' levels, Sam Seiden terminology). (This is only another entry LOCATION). And all other entries thereafter would be our stacking positions.

One more thing -- catching pinbars -- always 'look to the left', be mindful of what's to the left and set alerts if you see a possible DB situation, surely can't hurt.

Am I on the right track?

Thanks!

--- 帖子 #619 ---
Thank your for your compliments.Glad to hear you enjoying it.

Location has to be very easy to spot by traders. That’s why we want to see a price action out of any wicks or range so mass psychology can pay attention and follow it easily.
Although price usually respects to the past s/r levels from very long time ago,in terms of “starting its move” price needs a relatively close s/r level for the same reason “should be easily spotted”.
See the chart #1.
So I don’t consider all the past s/r levels to determine my possible entry levels.
I want something recent, easy to spot which is most of the time being previous week’s high-low or fib levels and major lines(1.4,1.3,etc).
That’s why I ignore the longer s/r level in the previous chart to keep things simple to trade.As you can see It did not meet the above requirements,iIt was not overlapped with neither any of the fib levels, high/low of the last week nor a major line.
Also you can see that the last week’s candle was an “almost inside bar” candle. In this case, I highlighted the areas that I’d be noticing  during the week.chart#2..
1st arrow :low of the week overlapping %50 fib of the recent swing
2nd arrow:high of the week
3rd 61.8 fib leve of the recent swing overlapping with major line
4th same with 1st (put that by accident)
5th 38.2 fib of the recent swing
6th new s/r level formed in the present week.
I usually get 1 or 2 4hr setup candles during a week.That start real move.
However this week  we’ve had (chart#3) 26 4hr candles finished but only 4of them could be taken as setup candles (1 of them countertrade.If you take that out you get 3 4hr candles).But none worked out.
This is all about trading itself.Sometimes you get 1 signal and a 500 pip quick move after that but sometimes “like this week” you get 3 signals but no significant move.Its like fishing so we have to be patient fishermen.

You're on the right track.Keep analysing previous moves and ask yourself which price action started the move..Thats very key to improve your trading skills.After you pass this stage you'll be spotting very easily and hearing that candles talking to you (not because you lost your mind by then)

Hi Cfabian:

I am new to the method, so please consider that when reading my response.

I would not have taken that trade. Here's why:

1. Rather than using the W1, H4, and M5 charts, it looks like you've used the D1, H1, and M5 charts.  I am not convinced that the price action on the H1 is nearly as reliable as price action on the H4.  I would have waited for more reliable PA on a higher timeframe.

2. It looks like your setup and entry candles on the M5 where at the beginning of a new H4 period.   I believe that Nomask has warned use to be extra caution when H4 candles are changing.

3.  I think you chose a good SL.

Best of luck with your trading.  I know that I have learned a lot since I started reading this thread.

--- 帖子 #676 ---
You can sit and watch if you like....good to do if you are still getting a feel for price action in the early stages (like first 6 months). If you've got price action down to a science and feel comfortable with your particular method and have expanded to playing multiple currency pairs sitting and watching becomes prohibitive and you'd want to set up alerts to your cell phone when price reaches a certain area e.g. just before it reaches your 38, 50, and 61 Fib....like 10-20 pips prior...for each respective pair.....or for areas around stalls/pennants looking for breakouts up or down etc. etc.

There are a number of dif ways to do this depending on your platform and cell phone service provider. Here is a link with some good info on the subject...

http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...postcount=4102

--- 帖子 #696 ---
I don't pay attention if i'm drawing it in the direction of the move.I just need to see fib levels..%0 or %100 no difference.

Don't get confused by applying fib..

the principle is that we put fib on "the setup candles"all the time..

If the week before last week setup candle is still intact yes we keep the fib on it since we do not have a more recent price action..

--- 帖子 #709 ---
Hi Jason,

Patience is a virtue, especially in this business, I have day job and therefore I am in the same boat as you. I got burnt too when I first tried out this method with my personal twist, i.e. take every green candle as set up (guilty as charged ). because I felt that i may be missing the boat. however, what I realized is this, by taking a green candle that is not the bottom turn of the retracement or a breakout candle, I am risking more in the sense that the bull will run out of steam sooner, but most importantly, that my position have higher chance of getting taken out when retracement happens. vice versa for short

i think nomask's quote fits nicely here

There is a good saying, if the boat already left the dock, dont jump into the ocean swimming after it, wait for the next one. (I am most reaffirming this to myself, by nature, I am a very impulsive person. -.-)

i dont know you what your time zone is, but I am in the eastern time zone, so i get 3 closing times. US close candle as setup, watch the close of half of the asian session. go to sleep, wake up in the morning and watch the close of half the london session, go to work. LOL

due to my time constraints, I also watch the daily close, and use that as a set up candle as well, although not in the same way as nomask's method, but the concept is the same, wait for a good daily close set up bar in the direction of the trend, and I use 15min bars in this case for entry, and reduce my normal lot size by half.

I currently have a eur/usd position at 1.42251, and the entry occurred in the asian session, double bottom 15 min pin bar. as you see, I had to baby sit it for a while before it took off. but the set up candle was from the us open but the entry was in the asian session.

My advice to you is, if the market doesn't want to go down, it is very likely it wants to go up and vice versa. but we need a confirmation of it going up before looking for entries. and we will never know where the opportunity for entry will be (pinbar, engulfing, 2 bar reversal, etc).  I agree, asian market is more calm and less violitity, thats why i also look at the 15min chart during the asian session for entry points, with reduced lot size, I see it as the price you pay for 10 more minutes of information.

again, I am a newbie, and these are just my take on it. hope it has helped you a bit.

--- 帖子 #715 ---
Hello Jason.I hope you demo traded this method before trading it live..

Its not because you need to see if you can trade it but also you need your trading data/performance to set your money management rules..

Personally I risk very small lot size for every position..

I use 0.1 lot for each 5k

and my average loss is 6-8 pips..that makes my each trade with 6-8$ risk or % 0,15.

So I need about 35 consecutive loss to spend %5 of my capital.

considering the fact that I get average 4 trades per week.

This could take me probably 7-8 weeks to lose that 35 trades.

I don't mean to make you feel worse.I'm just trying to show how this method in fact such a conservative way of trading.

We should find this method very boring and simple..If not then there is something wrong.

We either overtrade or overexpose.

One more important thing.

Lets say you started trading with 10k and lost your 1k but realized that you made so many mistakes while losing that and now you recently trading better.Then forget about that 1k and take it as your training fee and focus on that 9k as your initial capital..Because if you get stuck with the idea of that you lost 1k you won't be able to overcome emotional hurdle.

We definetly need human skills to trade (thats why I don't believe in ea trading) but with no emotion (as low as possible).

But when I look back now I can see that I could've been able to double my account easily if I was able to avoid all the sloppy entries and trading full time.

You may have some period of months over 20% profit of your account and some other months at b.e or small loss..Its all up to how patient and consistent you can be in trading.

--- 帖子 #742 ---
Finally, do any of you close any positions if they reverse at the median line? The median line is quickly approaching for EUR/USD.

The answer for me is yes only if there is a clear signal to do so.  This is not the only method I trade but this is great for portfiolio diversification.  Also as it moves in my favor(ex. 100pips) I shave a VERY small percentage of profit off so if it turns around and hit breakeven in reality I close in profit.   My overall picture is to let the market run as far as it wants run dispite what I think or analize.  Nomask and I(also others here) have the same mindset that price is king.  Shaving off is NOT based on the method, but it works for the accounts I manage.  The main thing is believing in yourself and others using this with great results.  Start at page one if you need too.  Stay away from the "bells and whistle" indicators unless they are alerts.  See what story the charts price is telling you in relation to S/R.  I have grown to realize in my years at forex is one major factor.  I had to release my control over to the market(and what I think I knew) and follow what price is doing.

Hang in there bro at this point even though there are 4 pairs that could be setting up next week stick with one this week and focus on skills of low risk entry to breakeven until you get into a groove.  Then add pairs.  Remember to find the hindsight(direction) and trade in that direction.  One you could look at is the A/U as it close above median line per nomask charts.  The story looks better there at the moment.

Good luck this week

--- 帖子 #815 ---
Now I can finalize explaining the method with this post..

So far I covered everything that I look for when taking a trade but not the part of experience which you'll gain by the time no matter what trading method you trade..

stick to the rules of being

patient

disciplined

confident and clear.

There is no such thing fixed percent of gain every week..
Evidence:Market does not move in a certain amount of pips every week or day.

There is no fixed reward/risk ratio
Evidence:You never know how many pips market is willing to move.

My humble advice would be do your best in terms of low risk entries and leave rest to the market.

As some of you already know that when I first started this thread i got into a nice setup which I've been holding since and now it passed the 1000 pips level.

If you're new to the thread you can check that detailed trading setup and live entry I made in the earlier pages of the thread.

We are now at either final of or renewing stage of our position.
You are good to close it with 1000 pips profit
as well as waiting this week to end to see if this will be another bullish setup that we might want to target further entering new positions along with our old position alive.

Its all up to you.your gain is directly connected to your risk size but you also need to grow your account.

Our target is riding such moves with more than one position .

I could only have 1 position on for this move and this is just because its my bad and busy period of my other works.

my decision would be that I'd be watching the market closely and see if its making another bullish setup by the end of this week.If not I may close my position and look for the next move.

But If I had more than one position by now I'd diversify some and leave the rest in.

THIS IS A DOT.

You have analysis,entry rules and exit in your hands.

No need to make things complicated.

REMEMBER IF YOU CONFUSE YOURSELF

OR TRY TO CATCH EVERY SINGLE MOVE

YOU WILL LOSE YOUR MONEY BIG TIME.

You have witnessed that its possible to catch over 1000 pips by risking 6 pips..

This is the fact and I'd suggest anyone to think about it.

The Market (big guys,brokers,stop hunters,fund managers,banks) want you to risk more.

Don't fall into their trap.

Wait until you see the direction they're headed (Its weekly timeframe)

Wait until you see something medium term traders might be interested to take action (4hr timeframe)

Wait until you see something good for day traders to give us a initial boost to move our entry to break even (5 min timeframe)

By doing this you are being long,medium and short term trader at the same time.

Doens't that just sound cool

Good luck all and thank you all for your continued interest to this thead.

--- 帖子 #901 ---
I have a lot of screentime issues due to my job, my girl, and the need to sleep every now and again . One thing to consider is that you could get a demo from a broker that's GMT+1, 2, +3, etc. I'm fairly certain there is a new four hour candle every hour depending on the broker. I use Alpari, FXDD, and MBT. I've heard FXPro has another 4 hour candle time, but I haven't verified this. The nice thing about Nomask's method, is that once you see the retrace setup on the weekly/four hour, then you can really choose any entry method that you please and hold it for the big moves. There are quite a few 15M entry methods on the forums (Sonic, EOHater/Ken Lee, to name a couple). I am trying to demo the two I just mentioned, but find myself going back to simple 5M moves based on Nomask's teachings. There are a lot of entry methods on the Equity Millipede thread, as well. If you have only an hour before you have to go to work, on the 15M you essentially have 4 candles to enter from instead 12 on the 5M. I prefer the latter. Having the multiple broker charts seems to help finding the right place to enter when you're pressed for time, though.

I hope this helps, man. Happy pips!

--- 帖子 #960 ---
You're welcome Greg.

You're right that I've been talking about overtrading a lot..Because its very important yet I can't talk enough of it.

There are two main reasons behind why you should avoid overtrading.

1.It makes you lose money by making sloppy entries.

2.This is even more important.You miss real opportunities because of overtrading.

Lets say you made 3-4 really bad entries (and you know you been overtrading).You just felt you must trade and lost quite amount of your capital.

But right after your overtrading you get a real opportunity (very simple,low risk,easy to catch) but this time you're scared to take it because of your previous losses.

So overtrading damages you both financially and psychologically which is the end of story for a trader.

--- 帖子 #961 ---
Hmmm.  Ain't that the truth.  That is exactly what happens. And the one you don't pull the trigger on is the one you really should have been on. Great advice.

--- 帖子 #966 ---
to me there is not much difference between engulfing bars and outside bars as long as they both mean that the direction of the price significantly changed.I like both of them

I don't like inverted hammers,harami,doji kind of things...Because they're not easy to spot.

Engulfing,outside,pinbar and 3 bar reversals my favourite.

in the attached chart,price played as per our hindsight but in the eastern timezone (not mine)..I hope some of you guys were able to take advantage of that pinbar.

--- 帖子 #1104 ---
That's kinda funny...I did something similar. I figure, on a daily basis price seems to move at least 100 pips, applying the same theory that if it crosses and closes beyond one 00 price, it's likely to head to the next...perhaps on it's way to the next major 0000 price.

Being that forex is so fractal...meaning you can't really tell a 5 min chart apart from an hourly chart without a labeled x & y axis...then it stands to reason that moving down a couple of time frames proportionately should work too.

I'm hoping it would be a benefit to those confined to a specific trading session due to their geographical time zone, such as mine which is PST zone. That makes my prime trading time during the Asian session and I usually miss setups using Nomask's timeframes because they usually occur during other sessions when I'm sleeping or at work.

However, that's only a theory and the only way to tell is to try it out....in demo at first. I'm applying the method as explained by Nomask except instead when price crosses and closes in relation to the 00 (100 pip) price levels, I'm using the Daily (hindsight), hourly and 5min charts.

--- 帖子 #1111 ---
All I can I say about overtrading is what has worked for me: previously I would trade exactly the same hours everyday which led to a subconscious feeling that I had to get at least a trade in per session and to generally taking less than optimal set-ups..

to counter this I stopped setting aside fixed hours and will now go to the platform at irregular times -if there is something eye-catching then I watch more and sometimes trade -if not I switch off and do something else instead. This has led to less time in front of the computer (with all the benefits that entails), FAR fewer trades per week and much better percentages of money-making (and even more non-money-losing)trades .

best of luck with this tricky issue,

greg

--- 帖子 #1119 ---
The reason we do not take profit at 60-80 pips (or even 170, like Nomasks NZD/USD BE trade posted earlier) is because this is our mindset:

- We'd rather a position die at break even then taking profit before the major (or minor, if you must) lines. In the case of EUR/USD, that would mean 1.35, 1.40, 1.45, and 1.50.

-60-80 pips in the bag sounds nice, but what if that position goes on to fulfill it's weekly momentum (per this method) and nets you 500-1000 pips? Nomask has already stated that with a .02% risk per trade, one run of 1000 pips added 20% to his starting capital. That's .02, not 2%. If it were 2%, that same position would have added 200% to his capital when he cashed it out. (Note: I'm not suggesting this amount of risk)

-Back to the 60-80 pips example: If you cash out at 60 pips and then reenter, then you have a GREATER CHANCE that your position will die at breakeven on the retrace. This is exactly what we're trying to avoid.

-To summarize, get an entry in at low risk (5-10 pips SL) on the 5 minute chart and let it run awhile, move it to break even and then forget about it. If it runs for 1000 pips toward the intended direction, then cash it out if you want.

I'm not trying to be argumentative or abrasive toward you (or Tania), but this is the entire point of Nomask's methodology. To talk about signals or "when to take profit" are conflicting with the original poster's method. If there is anything we are "supposed" to get from this method (or Graeme's) it's that multiple position on the "long term" will net you many more pips for much less risk. Did you think a risk:return of 1:200 was possible? It is with the ideas from this thread. I invite you to check out the Equity Millipede thread, as well, of which Nomask was a great contributor. Graeme has multiple positions riding long term (monthly) trends and they net him thousands of net new pips PER WEEK. Nomask (and Graeme) show what can be accomplished by looking at the "big picture".

I hope this clears some things up. I wish you all the best in your trading.

Hi Nomask/Everyone,

Its been a while since I posted on FF. I have been busy with other business/work commitments. I have still been following Graeme's thread with interest.

I just wanted to congratulate Nomask on this thread. I had been working on something similar but was trading too many timeframes and also over-trading.

I just want to share something that may help a few first time traders.

Last year I ruptured 2 discs in my back and had several months off work. It was around the time Graeme started his thread(Building an Equity Millepede). I spent the majority of my time laid on the floor reading Graemes thread and trying to put all the valuable lessons into trading. I was by all intents and purposes a full time trader. I had no success.

What I realise now about that period in my trading was that looking at charts all day can be counter productive. You end up seeing opportunities where there are none.

Everybody has the dream of been a succesfull full time trader and leaving there day jobs, but in my experience your day job/business can help your trading by preventing you from over-trading.

Can you imagine the discipline required to sit in-front of the computer all day and not pull the trigger? I believe its almost impossible.

Far better to check occasionally as per this method and if there is a set up then sit down and focus, if not then walk away.

On a side not I am currently short the Euro and +300pips. I just attempted another position after the 4hr candle closed below 1.4 it started to go against me on the 5 min so I closed out for -5pips. I will try again if it comes back up to test 1.4 or a fib level.

Happy Trading to all and keep up the good work Nomask.

Regards,

Ben

--- 帖子 #1168 ---
Simple and Jason,

Thanks for your comments. Although I agree with you, I was thinking of a way to "scalp" the market with 30-50 pip trades while our long term setup arises. Think it this way... if we can accumulate some pips by short term trading, then we can risk all or part of those same profits to build a more leveraged entry on the long term, by still risking 10 - 15 pips.

i.e. if get 60 pips by scalping, then on your long term setup you can risk your 15 or so pips at double size, meaning you're risking 30 pips of your scalping profit, without compromising your "original capital". Just a way of building cushion.

--- 帖子 #1169 ---
I guess that you have also read Graeme (a.k.a pipeasy on FF)`s thread?

Although a resolutely very, very long-term trader, when Graeme enters his trades (at least a good many of them) he is looking for set-ups when the price will quickly move in his favour and where he can have a very tight stop-loss. After it moves in his favour of course he is not looking to take profit immediately so he is not`scalping` but he certainly could apply the same set-ups and entries to scalping with great success if he wanted.

Graeme stresses many times the importance of practicing on demo for six months picking the right set-ups (on a 5 min.timeframe)  and having a fixed 20 pip SL and 20 pip PT. He feels that once you are consistently right over half the time then you are ready to trade by picking really good entries (obviously key to scalping).

--- 帖子 #1184 ---
Cfabian, in addition to Nomask's reply I would like to share few hints I learnt from Pipeasy and other guys.

1. Almost engulfing = attracts higher risk, so entry is possible with lower lotsize or with same lotsize, realizing that there is a higher risk of fault for such entry.

2. "Anticipation" (for details - check Pipeasy's thread).

When you see a bar, unclosed yet, or closing near the open of the prev. opposite bar, you can anticipate that price move was not sporadic and rather than not, it'll continue running in the direction of last move.

Beautiful example was in Pipeasy's thread, when if we see a current H4 or H1 candle, unclosed yet, near the level where it engulfes prev. opposite candle, we can take this fact as a valid signal to go to lower TF for entry, but assuming we're taking higher risk, as candle is still not closed.

3. Entry zones - as Pipeasy taught, we're not looking for exact pip for entry, instead we're looking for certain key areas near important levels.

It's "ALMOST" everywhere in life. It means there is a risk everywhere. Our target is to identify where we can accept the risk, at which cost, and what for. Not always risk taking is good. Out of market is also a good alternative from time to time. Overconfidence attracts lower profit. Not enough confidence attracts unjustified high risk.

--- 帖子 #1190 ---
Hello, guys.

On this week. Few facts to consider:

1. It's a start of new month.

2. It's a NFP release week.

Assumption: ranging moves with no clear established direction, or very low trend strength.

Result: positions opened are likely to end as losses or died at BE.

Next week we will see how market will interpret this week NFP and, possibly, make a choice to continue current direction (continuation of upmove), or to continue with last monthly candle, which is bearish.

So, IMHO we have a contradiction in hindsights, which is bearish for MN and bullish for WK. Pipeasy taught to avoid such pairs with contradicting hindsights, because this contradiction means price may go either way. But also he taught to "participate" - make low risk entries at suitable opportunities, in order to catch the train in the beginning of new trend.

Personally, I find trading in a week of NFP is purely overtrading, discouraging and creating anxiety and frustration on most occasions. Chances ARE NOT in our favor most of the times. Rarely when NFP week has a clear established trend, which continues by Friday NFP release with even more move in that trend direction. That pre-NFP days trend means that traders were anticipating NFP results and bought on rumors many days before the actual NFP release.

If you have 2 undesirable outcomes which makes you feel worse?*

1. You get edgy about a trade (possibly after a few back-to-back losses) and take profit of , say, 80 pips, then shortly after see that if you had stayed in you would be hundreds of pips in profit and rising...

2. You keep your S.L. at B.E. and then get stopped out -making no profit at all.

I  believe that getting the right mindset and training youself to take option 2 over option 1 is one of the key battles of this thread`s followers .

I am always looking for real-life-trading examples as to why sticking to your guns and taking either option 2 or infinite profits is better than option 1 overall -- fortunately most weeks will throw up more than 1 concrete eample of this which helps put steel into my backbone..

--- 帖子 #1196 ---
You've hit the nail right on the head. If you do #1 and take that 80 pips to the bank, it won't usually pay for the pips that it cost to make the long term positions/legs that you require to succeed. How many failed entries are paid for in full from one position cashed out at 1000 pips? That's the beauty of this method.

Also, please do as I say, not as I do. By the end of April, I was net profitable in my account due to waiting to cash out one position until the big EUR/USD move to the minor line of 1.45. I also traded a lot less at the time. Nomask (where are you, Master???) would have been proud of each low-risk entry that I took.

Fast forward to NOW: I've taken some small wins and MANY losses and in the end, I've lost a fair amount of money. Even with the overtrading, the "revenge" trades, increasing my lot size unnecesarrily, and the frequent times in the month of May that I felt confident enough to place a trade that Nomask wouldn't have done in a million years, I still would have had all of my losses paid for with ONE big move. Although I was net profitable by the end of April, if I let my 2 other positions run to that minor line of 1.45 instead of closing them out at 100 pips in April (because "no one became broke taking profits", right?), I would be net profitable right now.

The moral of this story is to listen to the original poster's ideas. And listen to Graeme, too. The small chunks of the pie won't pay the operational costs of your business. Let it die on BE (not BE +1) and take your 500 pips (minor line, if you must ) or 1000 pip (major line) position all the way to the bank. If a position dies at BE after reaching 200 pips, who cares? The position didn't want to "go the distance" for you so to hell with it!

I hope that I have learned my lesson this time. I deposited last week the amount that I lost for more available margin and another go-round. I wouldn't have had to do that if I just followed scenario #2.

The good news? Last week I added these 3 positions with Nomask's method:

As of today:

short USD/JPY: +208 pips

long EUR/USD: +295 pips

short USD/CAD: +56 pips

My vow to you, myself, and Charlie Sheen:

I will let them all die on BE before I close them out in the rare chance that they keep going in my desired direction. I will also keep my lot size constant and increase the amount of my positions in the market. I have also found that the more I trade, the more I lose. So I will only recognize a 4 hour candle that basically screams "NOMASK ENTRY" to me and everyone else here. No more taking chances. No more throwing sh*t against a wall and hoping it sticks. I think I've learned my lesson now.

I hope this truly personal post helps someone come to this realization before losing their shirt in this market. I also hope that by publically posting my promise to myself and this thread, that it solidifies my commitment to keep trading this amazing method that requires nothing but discipline, patience and a level head to become extremely profitable.

Happy pips to each of you!

Hi All

I know this is not an thread with lots of indi's but I was having problems drawing my fibs for weekly / 4hr nicely onto my 5m chart

hence this indicator

you can specify the period you want the fibs for (4hr, daily, weekly etc.)

and you place it on the chart that you use to enter, eg. 5m

it will always use the last closed bar of the period specified.

one parameter i am not sure about the default for is the xb_Move.HiLo - this moves the Hi/Lo of the fib based on PA that occurred after the fib candle closed.

Reason I am confused is that Nomask posted twice regarding this with different answers (post 216 - move the fibo, post 220 - do not move the fibo) - so I am not sure what is the correct setting

Nomask - if you are reading this please could you advise.

You can add the indicator multiple times without problem (it uses the fibo period in the fibo name) - but best to use different colors.

It always goes top to bottom as it only plots the major levels of 38.2, 50 & 61.8

On a new bar of the fibo period it will automatically create a new one.

Regards

John

second is -like you said-being prepared for both directions all the time...

this is just an endless battle between bulls and bears and sometimes we get lost in the middle of the battle and forget which side we were fighting with.Between our major lines its battlefiled where you get all dust and mess that sometimes you can't even see anything.When it happens best thing to do is retreat to the major line and wait until all the dust settle.

--- 帖子 #1266 ---
Hello Zusch,
I’m getting philosophical about trades I enter around ‘00s which, I hope, is a healthy state to get to.  I used to think I had to get in at ’00.  As Graeme says, his “biggest helper” when considering entries at any point is whether price is coming up or coming down from ’00, and if we enter in the right direction at ’00 we know that price might well proceed to the next ’00.
I place price behaviour at ‘00s into roughly 5 types:
a)    It charges straight through and doesn’t look back
b)    It bounces and departs in the direction it came from
c)    It bounces and then moves through
d)    It moves through and returns for a touch before proceeding on its way
e)    It hangs around for a long time after your entry, pushing through in both directions, and then it’s 50/50 as to whether you’ll have a successful trade.
I’ve seen this behaviour on 15m to H4 depending on the pace of the market that day/hour.
Either early in Nomask’s thread or in Graeme’s thread, some guy said that he only (he said “and I mean only”) trades on support turning to resistance or vice versa, as in (d) above. Perhaps I’m stressing myself by wanting to be on as many winning trades as possible, but I couldn’t limit myself to a strategy such as his where there will be relatively fewer opportunities.
I tend to expect some price action at ’00.  (I used to grieve when (a) happens.)  I’ve concluded that if there’s recognisable price action at ‘00, I’ll trade accordingly, but if there isn’t, I’ll catch the tide later when there’s price action beyond  ’00.
I’m intrigued by your phrase “simple candlestick patterns on round numbers are the most effective indicators just because of their simplicity.”  Would you mind expanding on that please?  Is your perspective anywhere near mine?

Thanks,

Kan

--- 帖子 #1268 ---
I think we are on the same page. I used to look for support and resistance on daily charts, but I had no real consistent way of identifying them. Round numbers however are very simple to define. Candlestick patterns (such as pinbars/engulfing patterns/3 bar reversal) are a little more subjective but much more easy to define than head and shoulders for example. Pinbars in my opinion are the best candlestick pattern. Here are the links to basic pinbar strategy:
http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...7&d=1236359305
http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...chmentid=43134

From your list of possibilities I like to trade scenarios B and D. I am trying to work in scenario E as moves out of tight ranges usually are the fastest moves. So using our weekly hindsight I take trades off of candlestick patterns on these round numbers. I cannot stress how important it is that your weekly chart is telling you what direction the trend is. If you are simply trading 4 hour pinbars on 100 pip levels both ways you will get a lot of signals and it will more than likely cost you a lot of money. Fewer, higher quality trades is the goal. This has all been said before by Nomask and others in this thread and if you haven't read through the entire thread yet I strongly recommend it just so you don't miss anything.

I certainly hope this post helped!

Zusch, I certainly understand your and others point of view about H & S patterns and other formations for that matter. Be honest with you I try not to rely to heavily on them, but when I see them I take note and try to understand their behavior especially if I see them in the  lower 5 min  and  upper 4hr timeframes  as I saw the other day on usdjpy.  Yesterday didn't end up forming which was the case , but  I like to point it out just for feedback be it positive or negative. I look at the proximity of the price to the mid levels also. I also agree with you about interpreting candles, be it individual or formations. Like everthing we do here in this thread or other threads I know you 'll have to agree that as traders we have to  weigh objectivity ( Price Action confirmations ) with subjectivity ( intuition and experience ).
