--- 帖子 #1276 ---
Cfabian

Here is how I see it. Last week or two I had a bias long noted by the price bounce off the previous resistance(white line and arrows). Another indication was price also bounce off of the 4000 level broke through 4500 headed north but failed and closed below 4500 , so that was why I had a short hindsight. The close below 4500 gave me the short hindsight and I waited according to the method and got in. Yes engulfing are my no brainer entry but they will not always line up as you want them too. It was close enough for me. (I use other analysis also). Use discretion if it looks good get in. According to my eagle eye skills we might be good down to 1.3050 so you my have time. HERE IS THE BEAUTY OF THIS METHOD. We should not care which way the market is going if it tells us short or long we go. Same for price target(we have none) . I have target because I am managing other folks hard earn cashola, but in my account I want all the market has to offer. We either breakeven or let it run until 1000 pip are hit or it tells us its turning around. Hope this helps Nomask may explian it better.

Summary:  My long died at breakeven the candle closed below 4500 so  I went short.

--- 帖子 #1277 ---
Guys, on EU, don't forget few things to consider:

1. Prev. month was bearish (not engulfing, but still), low is much lower the open of month before.

2. Prev. week was bearish (not engulfing, but still).

3. Mon and Tue PA on H1 and H4 - very lazy, candles were looking more like a retracement to the main trend, not like a full trend full bodied candles.

4. Long positions opened were dying on BE pretty much this month.

Conclusion => bears getting more power this month, and few bullish weeks were just an upper wick on monthly candle, which now looking bearish.

Hi all,

I wanted to get this out so I can enjoy the weekend.  I scanned the charts with low spread and with potential opportunity for the coming weeks and USD/CAD and USD/JPY is what I found.  I will be looking for dollar strength(from a technical prospective).

My currency story:
USD/CAD(monthly)-The technical story tells me we are at a double price bottom with a potential long bias which dated back 11/1/2007.  After this it went north.  At this point price is hanging in the wind with no support nor resistance to propel from.  A good place to keep an eye on price is the 1.000 level.  It would be nice to see it break through close then open above for the new week so we can find a low risk entry.
FYI-I looked at this on the monthly because this had the better story

USD/JPY(Weekly)-The technical story tells me we have a lot of selling pressure but if it can stay above 80.00 we may soon be looking for buy entries due to the double price bottom which dated back 6/1/1994.  After this it went north.  At this point price needs to break the trendlines and have a GOOD bullish candle to get my attention.  This pair has not faired well with me for the last 2 weeks and that is why.  Currently it is range bound.  85.00 is the true break area. A good place to keep an EYE on price is the 82.00 level(early bird chases the worm).
FYI-If we get a signal and we are riding it there is VERY strong resistance at the 88.50 level

Final note:  Because we are so close to the 1.000 level on the CAD  I would look at this one first.  Have a good weekend

PPS:  If anyone notice other charts or different analysis post it.  Adios!

--- 帖子 #1387 ---
I am still new to this method but I think I can help you with your question.

We get our bias from last weeks weekly candle and we do not change our bias untill we get a new weekly candle.

So last week big bull candle passing through and closing above .9 major line. My bias is to go long and I will only be looking for oportunitys to go long this week.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

I placed my fibo on last weeks candle and moved down to 4hr charts. The zone I have painted yellow (38-62 fibo levels) is where I am waiting and watching for price action to tell me it is time to go long. I normaly only go for engulfing or a pinbar formations.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

So even though this pair has crossed below the .9 major line it has not gone past the 62% fibo level and we can still be waiting and watching for oportunitys to buy.

Bias is decided at the start of the week and we do not change our bias durring the week. I hope this was helpful.

I've been having a debate with myself the last couple weeks between staying with New York time or switching to London time. I know you've said Nomask that it doesn't matter overall but I just can't seem to convince myself of that. I think its a fact that the most likely positions to survive are opened at the beginning of whatever time frame you are looking at (beginning of week/day/4 hour bar). Unfortunately for U.S. traders this means very early mornings. So my logic to picking to display my bars in the London time zone is that more eyes are watching in that time zone with many Americans are still asleep (I'll be awake). I just feel as my entries (even if they get to B/E) are going to die on retraces simply because of the time of day of which I am entering. This last trade I took on AUDUSD is really bugging me because I was taken out on simple sideways action. Had I been on London time I would have gotten in earlier and still be alive in the trade today. I know one trade can't influence my decisions but I've seen this happen time and time again. I'm not sure if I've been clear enough in this post so sorry if I caused any confusion.

I'd appreciate it if someone who uses London time could post their 4 hour EURUSD so I can compare.

--- 帖子 #1460 ---
Selym,

I keep re-reading the first post on this thread.  Nomask makes a few key points about the "approach" (its not really a system in my opinion) that he uses.

1. He only trades EUR/USD.  Focusing on one pair makes it easier to concentrate.  I've chosen to look at a few others, but nothing exotic.

2. We look to enter with very tight stops, so that if we are right we are highly rewarded, and if not we lose a very small amount.  10 pips is the most he would ever risk.

3. Nomask uses the 5 minute charts for entry, but did say that you could use 15 minute charts as well.  The key is to see a move through a major line on the weekly, then look for P/A with fibs on 4HR, and then look for a smaller "entry" timeframe to hit a fib from the 4HR.  Really, you could enter just based on the 4HR P/A if you know how to properly use fib levels.

I was also trying to buy CHF after the move through .8000.  I was stopped out for a loss of 10 pips, not a problem.  This tells us that CHF hasn't decided whether to keep its major bear trend, or whether it is ready to reverse and start climbing above .8000.  But once it makes its mind up, it will be ready to go to .70 or to .90.  In the mean time, I've been doing well with EUR shorting it from 1.45, with the target of it going to 1.4000.

I'm just a newbie with regard to this trading approach, but I have succeeded in removing all other indicators from my charts, and I believe that this has already improve my trading.

I just stumbled unto this thread. It looks very nice... I quickly jumped to the last page just to see it is still going, but, Its a shame that it looks like this thread has gone quiet? Perhaps, everything we need to know about it has already been posted; hence no need to add more.

At first glance it reminds me of Quarters Theory by Ilian Yotov, and I was looking to see whether someone is trading applying that theory. Then I found this and it seems to be the closest to what appears to trade around this concept.

I look forward to going over the examples, particularly the honing in on H4 and M5 for entry.

Hopefully, too there will be more posts as eur/usd is trading in an increasingly interesting area. At this rate, we'll soon, be at the bottom of that 4000 pip rance/cycle.

peace, livindaylite
